<p><b>Darwin</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-au-Darwin.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/En-au-Darwin.ogg" title="En-au-Darwin.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i><b>DAR</b>-win</i></small></a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_capital_cities" title="List of Australian capital cities">capital city</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. Situated on the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Sea" title="Timor Sea">Timor Sea</a>, Darwin is the largest city in the sparsely populated Northern Territory, with a population of 145,916.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABS10YRS_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-ABS10YRS-1">[1]</a></sup> It is the smallest and most northerly of the Australian capital cities, and acts as the <a href="/wiki/Top_End" title="Top End">Top End</a>'s regional centre.</p>
<p>Darwin's proximity to South East Asia makes it a link between Australia and countries such as <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Highway" title="Stuart Highway">Stuart Highway</a> begins in Darwin, ending at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Augusta,_South_Australia" title="Port Augusta, South Australia">Port Augusta</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>. The city itself is built on a low bluff overlooking the harbour. Its <a href="/wiki/List_of_Darwin_suburbs" title="List of Darwin suburbs">suburbs</a> spread out over some area, beginning at <a href="/wiki/Lee_Point,_Northern_Territory" title="Lee Point, Northern Territory">Lee Point</a> in the north and stretching to <a href="/wiki/Berrimah,_Northern_Territory" title="Berrimah, Northern Territory">Berrimah</a> in the east. Past <a href="/wiki/Berrimah,_Northern_Territory" title="Berrimah, Northern Territory">Berrimah</a>, the Stuart Highway goes on to Darwin's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satellite_city" title="Satellite city">satellite city</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palmerston,_Northern_Territory" title="Palmerston, Northern Territory">Palmerston</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Palmerston_suburbs" title="List of Palmerston suburbs">its suburbs</a>. The Darwin region, like the rest of the Top End, has a tropical climate, with a <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>. Prone to cyclone activity during the wet season, Darwin experiences heavy monsoonal downpours and spectacular lightning shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GUM_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-GUM-8">[8]</a></sup> During the dry season, the city is met with blue skies and gentle sea breezes from the harbour.</p>
<p>The greater Darwin area is the ancestral home of the <a href="/wiki/Larrakia" title="Larrakia">Larrakia</a> people. On 9 September 1839, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Beagle" title="HMS Beagle">HMS <i>Beagle</i></a> sailed into Darwin harbour during its surveying of the area. <a href="/wiki/John_Clements_Wickham" title="John Clements Wickham">John Clements Wickham</a> named the region "Port Darwin" in honour of their former shipmate <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>, who had sailed with them on the <a href="/wiki/Second_voyage_of_HMS_Beagle" title="Second voyage of HMS Beagle">ship's previous voyage</a> which had ended in October 1836. The settlement there became the town of <a href="/wiki/Palmerston,_Northern_Territory" title="Palmerston, Northern Territory">Palmerston</a> in 1869, and was renamed Darwin in 1911.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-urlDarwin_.E2.80.93_Northern_Territory_.E2.80.93_Australia_.E2.80.93_Travel_.E2.80.93_smh.com.au_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-urlDarwin_.E2.80.93_Northern_Territory_.E2.80.93_Australia_.E2.80.93_Travel_.E2.80.93_smh.com.au-9">[9]</a></sup> The city has been almost entirely rebuilt four times, following devastation caused by the 1897 cyclone, the 1937 cyclone, <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Darwin" title="Bombing of Darwin">Japanese air raids</a> during World War II, and <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Tracy" title="Cyclone Tracy">Cyclone Tracy</a> in 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCC_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-DCC-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2>Contents</h2>

<ul>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Darwin" title="History of Darwin">History of Darwin</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Darwin_History" title="Timeline of Darwin History">Timeline of Darwin History</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="History of the Northern Territory">History of the Northern Territory</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre_20th_Century">Pre 20th Century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre 20th Century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Aboriginal people of the <a href="/wiki/Larrakia" title="Larrakia">Larrakia</a> language group are the traditional custodians and the first inhabitants of the greater Darwin area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> They had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trading_routes" title="Trading routes">trading routes</a> with Southeast Asia (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macassan_contact_with_Australia" title="Macassan contact with Australia">Macassan contact with Australia</a>), and imported goods from as far afield as <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South</a> and Western Australia. Established <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Songlines" title="Songlines">songlines</a> penetrated throughout the country, allowing stories and histories to be told and retold along the routes. The extent of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shared_songlines&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shared songlines (page does not exist)">shared songlines</a> and history of multiple clan groups within this area is still contestable.</p>
<p>The Dutch visited Australia's northern coastline in the 1600s and landed on the <a href="/wiki/Tiwi_Islands" title="Tiwi Islands">Tiwi Islands</a> only to be repelled by the <a href="/wiki/Tiwi_people" title="Tiwi people">Tiwi peoples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The Dutch created the first European maps of the area. This accounts for the Dutch names in the area, such as <a href="/wiki/Arnhem_Land" title="Arnhem Land">Arnhem Land</a> and <a href="/wiki/Groote_Eylandt" title="Groote Eylandt">Groote Eylandt</a>. The first British person to see Darwin harbour appears to have been Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/John_Lort_Stokes" title="John Lort Stokes">John Lort Stokes</a> of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Beagle" title="HMS Beagle">HMS <i>Beagle</i></a> on 9 September 1839. The ship's captain, Commander <a href="/wiki/John_Clements_Wickham" title="John Clements Wickham">John Clements Wickham</a>, named the port after <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>, the British naturalist who had sailed with them both on the earlier <a href="/wiki/Second_voyage_of_HMS_Beagle" title="Second voyage of HMS Beagle">second expedition of the <i>Beagle</i></a>.</p>
<p>In 1863, the Northern Territory was transferred from <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> to South Australia. In 1864 South Australia sent <a href="/wiki/B._T._Finniss" title="B. T. Finniss">B. T. Finniss</a> north as Government Resident to survey and found a capital for its new territory. Finniss chose a site at Escape Cliffs, near the entrance to Adelaide River, about 60 km northeast of the modern city. This attempt was short-lived, however, and the settlement abandoned by 1865.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> On 5 February 1869, <a href="/wiki/George_Goyder" title="George Goyder">George Goyder</a>, the Surveyor-General of South Australia, established a small settlement of 135 people at Port Darwin between <a href="/wiki/Fort_Hill,_Darwin" title="Fort Hill, Darwin">Fort Hill</a> and the escarpment. Goyder named the settlement <a href="/wiki/Palmerston,_Northern_Territory" title="Palmerston, Northern Territory">Palmerston</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_Temple,_3rd_Viscount_Palmerston" title="Henry Temple, 3rd Viscount Palmerston">Lord Palmerston</a>. In 1870, the first poles for the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Overland_Telegraph_Line" title="Australian Overland Telegraph Line">Overland Telegraph</a> were erected in Darwin, connecting Australia to the rest of the world. The discovery of gold by employees of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Overland_Telegraph_Line" title="Australian Overland Telegraph Line">Australian Overland Telegraph Line</a> digging holes for telegraph poles at <a href="/wiki/Pine_Creek,_Northern_Territory" title="Pine Creek, Northern Territory">Pine Creek</a> in the 1880s spawned a gold rush which further boosted the young colony's development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[a]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[b]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[c]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 1872 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brigatine" title="Brigatine">brigatine</a> <i>Alexandra</i> was the first private vessel to set sail from an English port directly to Darwin many of whom were people coming to recently gold finds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early 1875 Darwin's <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white population</a> had grown to approximately 300 because of the gold rush. On 17 February 1875 the <a href="/wiki/SS_Gothenburg" title="SS Gothenburg">SS <i>Gothenburg</i></a> left Darwin <i>en route</i> for <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>. The approximately 88 passengers and 34 crew (surviving records vary) included government officials, circuit-court judges, Darwin residents taking their first <a href="/wiki/Furlough" title="Furlough">furlough</a>, and miners. While travelling south along the north Queensland coast, the <i>Gothenburg</i> encountered a cyclone-strength storm and was wrecked on a section of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Barrier_Reef" title="Great Barrier Reef">Great Barrier Reef</a>. Only 22 men survived, while between 98 and 112 people perished. Many passengers who perished were Darwin residents and news of the tragedy severely affected the small community, which reportedly took several years to recover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTLIB_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-NTLIB-20">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_begins">20th century begins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 20th century begins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Remains_of_the_Darwin_Post_Office.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="279" data-file-width="450" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Remains_of_the_Darwin_Post_Office.jpg/220px-Remains_of_the_Darwin_Post_Office.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Remains_of_the_Darwin_Post_Office.jpg/330px-Remains_of_the_Darwin_Post_Office.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Remains_of_the_Darwin_Post_Office.jpg/440px-Remains_of_the_Darwin_Post_Office.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LYONS_COTTAGE_-_DARWIN_-_NORTHERN_TERRITORY.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1993" data-file-width="3000" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/LYONS_COTTAGE_-_DARWIN_-_NORTHERN_TERRITORY.jpg/220px-LYONS_COTTAGE_-_DARWIN_-_NORTHERN_TERRITORY.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/LYONS_COTTAGE_-_DARWIN_-_NORTHERN_TERRITORY.jpg/330px-LYONS_COTTAGE_-_DARWIN_-_NORTHERN_TERRITORY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/LYONS_COTTAGE_-_DARWIN_-_NORTHERN_TERRITORY.jpg/440px-LYONS_COTTAGE_-_DARWIN_-_NORTHERN_TERRITORY.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LYONS_COTTAGE_-_DARWIN_-_NORTHERN_TERRITORY.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lyons Cottage, c. 1925, office of the British Australian Telegraph Company</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Darwin became the city's official name in 1911.</p>
<p>The period between 1911 and 1919 was filled with political turmoil, particularly with trade union unrest, which culminated on 17 December 1918. Led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harold_Nelson_(Australian_politician)" title="Harold Nelson (Australian politician)">Harold Nelson</a>, some 1000 demonstrators marched to <a href="/wiki/Government_House,_Darwin" title="Government House, Darwin">Government House</a> at Liberty Square in Darwin where they burnt an <a href="/wiki/Effigy" title="Effigy">effigy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="Administrator of the Northern Territory">Administrator of the Northern Territory</a> <a href="/wiki/John_A._Gilruth" title="John A. Gilruth">John Gilruth</a> and demanded his resignation. The incident became known as the '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darwin_Rebellion" title="Darwin Rebellion">Darwin Rebellion</a>'. Their grievances were against the two main Northern Territory employers: <a href="/wiki/Vestey_Group" title="Vestey Group">Vestey's Meatworks</a> and the federal government. Both Gilruth and the Vestey company left Darwin soon afterwards.</p>
<p>Around 10,000 Australian and other <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> troops arrived in Darwin at the outset of World War II, in order to defend Australia's northern coastline. On 19 February 1942 at 0957, 188 <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> warplanes <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Darwin" title="Bombing of Darwin">attacked Darwin</a> in two waves. It was the same fleet that had bombed <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>, though a considerably larger number of bombs were dropped on Darwin than on Pearl Harbor. The attack killed at least 243 people and caused immense damage to the town, airfields and aircraft. These were by far the most serious attacks on Australia in time of war, in terms of fatalities and damage. They were the first of <a href="/wiki/Air_raids_on_Australia,_1942%E2%80%9343" title="Air raids on Australia, 1942–43">many raids</a> on Darwin.</p>
<p>Darwin was further developed after the war, with sealed roads constructed connecting the region to <a href="/wiki/Alice_Springs" title="Alice Springs">Alice Springs</a> in the south and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Isa" title="Mount Isa">Mount Isa</a> in the south-east, and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Manton_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Manton Dam (page does not exist)">Manton Dam</a> built in the south to provide the city with water. On <a href="/wiki/Australia_Day" title="Australia Day">Australia Day</a> (26 January) 1959, Darwin was granted city status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="1970–present_day"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.93present_day">1970–present day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970–present day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 25 December 1974, Darwin was struck by <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Tracy" title="Cyclone Tracy">Cyclone Tracy</a>, which killed 71 people and destroyed over 70% of the town's buildings, including many old stone buildings such as the Palmerston Town Hall, which could not withstand the lateral forces generated by the strong winds. After the disaster, 30,000 people of a then population of 46,000 were evacuated, in what turned out to be the biggest airlift in Australia's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCC_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-DCC-10">[10]</a></sup> The town was subsequently rebuilt with newer materials and techniques during the late 1970s by the Darwin Reconstruction Commission, led by former <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> Lord Mayor <a href="/wiki/Clem_Jones" title="Clem Jones">Clem Jones</a>. A satellite city of <a href="/wiki/Palmerston,_Northern_Territory" title="Palmerston, Northern Territory">Palmerston</a> was built 20 km (12 mi) south of Darwin in the early 1980s.</p>
<p>On 17 September 2003 the <a href="/wiki/Adelaide%E2%80%93Darwin_railway" title="Adelaide–Darwin railway">Adelaide–Darwin railway</a> was completed, with the opening of the Alice Springs-Darwin standard gauge line.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_skyline.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="781" data-file-width="1500" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Darwin_skyline.jpg/220px-Darwin_skyline.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Darwin_skyline.jpg/330px-Darwin_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Darwin_skyline.jpg/440px-Darwin_skyline.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_skyline.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Darwin skyline from East Point in 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Darwin lies in the Northern Territory, on the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Sea" title="Timor Sea">Timor Sea</a>. The city proper occupies a low bluff overlooking <a href="/wiki/Darwin_Harbour" title="Darwin Harbour">Darwin Harbour</a>, flanked by Frances Bay to the east and Cullen Bay to the west. The remainder of the city is flat and low-lying, and coastal areas are home to recreational reserves, extensive beaches, and excellent fishing.</p>
<p>Darwin is closer to the capitals of five other countries than to the capital of Australia: Darwin is 3,137 kilometres (1,949 mi) away from <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dili" title="Dili">Dili</a> (East Timor) is 656 km (408 mi), <a href="/wiki/Port_Moresby" title="Port Moresby">Port Moresby</a> (Papua New Guinea) is 1,818 km (1,130 mi), <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a> (Indonesia) is 2,700 km (1,678 mi), <a href="/wiki/Bandar_Seri_Begawan" title="Bandar Seri Begawan">Bandar Seri Begawan</a> (Brunei) is 2,607 km (1,620 mi), and <a href="/wiki/Ngerulmud" title="Ngerulmud">Ngerulmud</a> (Palau) is 2,247 km (1,396 mi) from Darwin.</p>
<p>Even Malaysia and Singapore are only slightly farther away at 3,350 km (2,082 mi), as is <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> (Philippines) at 3,206 km (1,992 mi), and <a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a> (Solomon Islands) at 3,198 km (1,987 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ambon_Island" title="Ambon Island">Ambon</a>, Indonesia, is only 881 km (547 mi) away from Darwin.</p>
<p>Along with its importance as a gateway to Asia, Darwin also acts as an access point for the <a href="/wiki/Kakadu_National_Park" title="Kakadu National Park">Kakadu National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnhem_Land" title="Arnhem Land">Arnhem Land</a>, and northerly islands such as <a href="/wiki/Groote_Eylandt" title="Groote Eylandt">Groote Eylandt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tiwi_Islands" title="Tiwi Islands">Tiwi Islands</a>. As the largest city in the area, it provides services for these remote settlements.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_and_suburbs">City and suburbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: City and suburbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Darwin_suburbs" title="List of Darwin suburbs">List of Darwin suburbs</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Wards_and_Suburbs_of_Darwin,_Northern_Territory.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3375" data-file-width="3060" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Map_of_the_Wards_and_Suburbs_of_Darwin%2C_Northern_Territory.png/170px-Map_of_the_Wards_and_Suburbs_of_Darwin%2C_Northern_Territory.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Map_of_the_Wards_and_Suburbs_of_Darwin%2C_Northern_Territory.png/255px-Map_of_the_Wards_and_Suburbs_of_Darwin%2C_Northern_Territory.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Map_of_the_Wards_and_Suburbs_of_Darwin%2C_Northern_Territory.png/340px-Map_of_the_Wards_and_Suburbs_of_Darwin%2C_Northern_Territory.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Wards_and_Suburbs_of_Darwin,_Northern_Territory.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Darwin with suburbs</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Darwin and its suburbs spread in an approximately triangular shape, with the older south-western suburbs—and the city itself—forming one corner, the newer northern suburbs in another, and the eastern suburbs, progressing towards Palmerston, forming the third.</p>
<p>The older part of Darwin is separated from the newer northern suburbs by <a href="/wiki/Darwin_International_Airport" title="Darwin International Airport">Darwin International Airport</a> and Royal Australian Air Force Base. <a href="/wiki/Palmerston,_Northern_Territory" title="Palmerston, Northern Territory">Palmerston</a> is a satellite city 20 km (12 mi) south of Darwin that was established in the 1980s and is one of the fastest growing municipalities in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup> The rural areas of Darwin including <a href="/wiki/Howard_Springs,_Northern_Territory" title="Howard Springs, Northern Territory">Howard Springs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humpty_Doo,_Northern_Territory" title="Humpty Doo, Northern Territory">Humpty Doo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berry_Springs,_Northern_Territory" title="Berry Springs, Northern Territory">Berry Springs</a> are experiencing strong growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitchell_Street_Darwin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1177" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Mitchell_Street_Darwin.jpg/170px-Mitchell_Street_Darwin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Mitchell_Street_Darwin.jpg/255px-Mitchell_Street_Darwin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Mitchell_Street_Darwin.jpg/340px-Mitchell_Street_Darwin.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mitchell_Street_Darwin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mitchell Street in Darwin CBD</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Darwin's central business district is bounded by Daly Street in the north-west, McMinn Street in the north-east, Mitchell Street on the south-west and Bennett Street on the south-east. The CBD has been the focus of a number of major projects, including the billion dollar redevelopment of the Stokes Hill wharf waterfront area including a convention centre with seating for 1500 people and approximately 4,000 square metres (43,000 sq ft) of exhibition space. The development will also include hotels, residential apartments and public space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> The city's main industrial areas are along the Stuart Highway going towards Palmerston, centred on <a href="/wiki/Winnellie,_Northern_Territory" title="Winnellie, Northern Territory">Winnellie</a>. The largest shopping precinct in the area is <a href="/wiki/Casuarina_Square" title="Casuarina Square">Casuarina Square</a>.</p>
<p>The most expensive residential areas stand along the coast in suburbs such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Larrakeyah,_Northern_Territory" title="Larrakeyah, Northern Territory">Larrakeyah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brinkin,_Northern_Territory" title="Brinkin, Northern Territory">Brinkin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> despite the slight risk these low-lying regions face during cyclones and higher tides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup> The inner northern suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Millner,_Northern_Territory" title="Millner, Northern Territory">Millner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coconut_Grove,_Northern_Territory" title="Coconut Grove, Northern Territory">Coconut Grove</a> and the eastern suburb of <a href="/wiki/Karama,_Northern_Territory" title="Karama, Northern Territory">Karama</a> are home to lower-income households, although low-income Territory Housing units are scattered throughout the metropolitan area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup> The suburb of Lyon was an addition to the Northern Suburbs. Development and construction took place in 2009 and 2010 and became home for a number of affluent Darwin residents and local/recently posted military families above the rank of Sergeant or Flying Officer.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_1824.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="700" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Darwin_1824.jpg/220px-Darwin_1824.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Darwin_1824.jpg/330px-Darwin_1824.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Darwin_1824.jpg/440px-Darwin_1824.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_1824.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A wet season storm at night in January</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Darwin has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen <i>Aw</i></a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup> with distinct wet and dry seasons and the average maximum temperature is remarkably similar all year round. The dry season runs from about May to September, during which nearly every day is sunny, and afternoon humidity averages around 30%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DarwinAirportAWS_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-DarwinAirportAWS-31">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The driest period of the year, seeing only approximately 5 mm (0.20 in) of monthly rainfall on average, is between May and September. In the coolest months of June and July, the daily minimum temperature may dip as low as 14 °C (57 °F), but very rarely lower, and a temperature lower than 10 °C (50 °F) has never been recorded in the city centre. Outer suburbs away from the coast, however, can occasionally record temperatures as low as 5 °C (41 °F) in the dry season. For an exceedingly lengthy 147‑day period during the 2012 dry season, from 5 May to 29 September, Darwin recorded no precipitation whatsoever. Prolonged periods of no precipitation are common in the dry season in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Australia" title="Northern Australia">Northern Australia</a> (particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> and northern regions of <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>) although a no-rainfall event of this extent is rare. The 3pm dewpoint average in the wet season is at around 24.0 °C (75.2 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DarwinAirportAWS_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-DarwinAirportAWS-31">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Extreme temperatures at the Darwin Post Office Station have ranged from 40.4 °C (104.7 °F) on 17 October 1892 to 13.4 °C (56.1 °F) on 25 June 1891; while extreme temperatures at the Darwin Airport station (which is further from the coast and routinely records cooler temperatures than the post office station which is located in Darwin's CBD) have ranged from 38.9 °C (102.0 °F) on 18 October 1982 to 10.4 °C (50.7 °F) on 29 July 1942. The highest minimum temperature on record is 30.7 °C (87.3 °F) on 18 January 1928 for the post office station and 29.7 °C (85.5 °F) on both 25 November 1987 and 17 December 2014 for the airport station; while the lowest maximum temperature on record is 18.4 °C (65.1 °F) on 3 June 1904 for the post office station and 21.1 °C (70.0 °F) on 14 July 1968 for the airport station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DarwinAirportAWS_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-DarwinAirportAWS-31">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DarwinPO_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-DarwinPO-32">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The wet season is associated with <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a> and monsoon rains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup> The majority of rainfall occurs between December and March (the southern hemisphere summer), when thunderstorms are common and afternoon relative humidity averages over 70 percent during the wettest months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DarwinAirportAWS_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-DarwinAirportAWS-31">[28]</a></sup> It does not rain every day during the wet season, but most days have plentiful cloud cover; January averages under 6 hours of bright sunshine daily. Darwin's highest Bureau of Meteorology verified daily rainfall total is 367.6 millimetres (14.47 in), which fell when <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Australian_region_cyclone_season" title="2010–11 Australian region cyclone season">Cyclone Carlos</a> bore down on the Darwin area on 16 February 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup> February 2011 was also Darwin's wettest month ever recorded, with 1,110.2 millimetres (43.71 in) recorded for the month at the airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DarwinAirportAWS_31-4"><a href="#cite_note-DarwinAirportAWS-31">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The hottest month is November, just before the onset of the main rain season. The <a href="/wiki/Heat_index" title="Heat index">heat index</a> sometimes rises above 45 °C (113 °F), while the actual temperature is usually below 35 °C (95 °F), because of humidity levels that most would find uncomfortable. Because of its long dry season, Darwin has the second most daily average sunshine hours (8.4) of any Australian capital with the most sunshine from April to November; only Perth, Western Australia averages more (8.8). The sun passes directly overhead in mid October and mid February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average temperature of the sea ranges from 25.8 °C (78.4 °F) in July to 31.5 °C (88.7 °F) in December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin occupies one of the most lightning-prone areas in Australia. On 31 January 2002 an early-morning <a href="/wiki/Squall_line" title="Squall line">squall line</a> produced over 5,000 cloud-to-ground lightning strikes within a 60-kilometre (37 mi) radius of Darwin alone – about three times the amount of lightning that Perth, Western Australia, experiences on average in an entire year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GUM_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-GUM-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup></p>
