<p>In 2006, the largest ancestry groups in Darwin were <a href="/wiki/Australians" title="Australians">Australian</a> (42,221 or 36.9%), <a href="/wiki/English_Australians" title="English Australians">English</a> (29,766 or 26%), <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous Australians</a> (10,259 or 9.7%), <a href="/wiki/Irish_Australians" title="Irish Australians">Irish</a> (9,561 or 8.3%), <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Australians" title="Scottish Australians">Scottish</a> (7,815 or 6.8%), <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Australians" title="Chinese Australians">Chinese</a> (3,502 or 3%), <a href="/wiki/Greek_Australians" title="Greek Australians">Greek</a> (2,828 or 2.4%), and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Australians" title="Italian Australians">Italian</a> (2,367 or 2%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin's population is notable for the highest proportional population of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous Australians</a> of any Australian capital city. In the 2006 census 10,259 (9.7 per cent) of Darwin's population was Aboriginal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-06census_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-06census-43">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin's population changed after the Second World War. Darwin, like many other Australian cities, experienced influxes from Europe, with significant numbers of <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> during the 1960s and 1970s. Darwin also started to experience an influx from other European countries, which included the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, and many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup> A significant percentage of Darwin's residents are recent immigrants from South East Asia (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Australian" title="Asian Australian">Asian Australians</a> were 9.3% of Darwin's population in 2001).</p>
<p>Darwin's population comprises people from many ethnic backgrounds. The 2006 Census revealed that the most common places of birth for overseas migrants were the United Kingdom (3.4 per cent), New Zealand (2.1 per cent), the Philippines (1.4 per cent) and East Timor (0.9 per cent). 18.3 percent of the city's population was born overseas, which is less than the Australian average of 22%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-06census_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-06census-43">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin has a youthful population with an average age of 33 years (compared to the national average of around 37 years)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> assisted to a large extent by the military presence and the fact that many people opt to retire elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most common languages spoken in Darwin after English are <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Australian Aboriginal languages">Australian Aboriginal languages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-06census_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-06census-43">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Christianity has the most adherents in Darwin, with 56,613 followers accounting for 49.5 per cent of the population of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> The largest denominations of Christianity are <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> (24,538 or 21.5 per cent), <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a> (14,028 or 12.3 per cent) and <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodoxy</a> (2,964 or 2.6 per cent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup> Buddhists, Muslims, Hindus and Jews account for 3.2 per cent of Darwin's population. There were 26,695 or 23.3 per cent of people professing no religion.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_growth">Population growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Population growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Darwin is one of the fastest growing capital cities in Australia, with an annual growth rate of 2.6 per cent since the 2006 census. In recent years, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Palmerston" title="City of Palmerston">Palmerston</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shire_of_Litchfield" title="Shire of Litchfield">Litchfield</a> parts of the Darwin statistical division have recorded the highest growth in population of any <a href="/wiki/Local_government_areas_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="Local government areas of the Northern Territory">Northern Territory local government area</a> and by 2016 Litchfield could overtake Palmerston as the second largest municipality in metropolitan Darwin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup> It is predicted by 2021 that the combined population of both Palmerston and Litchfield would be 101,546 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Law and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly.jpg/220px-Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly.jpg/330px-Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly.jpg/440px-Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Legislative Assembly of the Northern Territory</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Northern_Territory.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Northern_Territory.JPG/220px-Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Northern_Territory.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Northern_Territory.JPG/330px-Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Northern_Territory.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Northern_Territory.JPG/440px-Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Northern_Territory.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Northern_Territory.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In the Legislative Assembly</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/City_of_Darwin" title="City of Darwin">Darwin City Council</a> (Incorporated under the Northern Territory Local Government Act 1993) governs the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Darwin" title="City of Darwin">City of Darwin</a> which takes in the CBD and the suburbs. The Darwin City Council has governed the City of Darwin since 1957. The Darwin City Council consists of 13 elected members, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor" title="Lord Mayor">Lord Mayor</a> and 12 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aldermen" title="Aldermen">aldermen</a>.</p>
<p>The City of Darwin electorate is organised into four electoral units or wards. The names of the wards are Chan, Lyons, Richardson, and Waters. The constituents of each ward are directly responsible for electing three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aldermen" title="Aldermen">aldermen</a>. Constituents of all wards are directly responsible for electing the Lord Mayor of Darwin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> The mayor is <a href="/wiki/Kon_Vatskalis" title="Kon Vatskalis">Kon Vatskalis</a> after council elections in August 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2017mayor_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-2017mayor-52">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rest of the Darwin area is divided into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_Government_Areas_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="Local Government Areas of the Northern Territory">2 local government areas</a>—the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Palmerston" title="City of Palmerston">Palmerston City Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Coomalie_Shire" title="Coomalie Shire">Shire of Coomalie</a>. These areas have elected councils which are responsible for functions delegated to them by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Territory_Government" title="Northern Territory Government">Northern Territory Government</a>, such as planning and garbage collection.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory_Legislative_Assembly" title="Northern Territory Legislative Assembly">Legislative Assembly of the Northern Territory</a> convenes in Darwin in the Northern Territory <a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Darwin" title="Parliament House, Darwin">Parliament House</a>. <a href="/wiki/Government_House,_Darwin" title="Government House, Darwin">Government House</a>, the official residence of the <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="Administrator of the Northern Territory">Administrator of the Northern Territory</a>, is located on The Esplanade.</p>
<p>Also located on the Esplanade is the <a class="external text" href="http://www.supremecourt.nt.gov.au/" rel="nofollow">Supreme Court of the Northern Territory</a>. Darwin has a <a class="external text" href="http://www.nt.gov.au/justice/ntmc" rel="nofollow">Magistrate's Court</a> also which is located on the corner of Cavenagh and Bennett Streets quite close to the Darwin City Council Chambers. Darwin's police force are members of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory_Police" title="Northern Territory Police">Northern Territory Police</a> Force. Darwin's Mitchell Street, with its numerous pubs, clubs and other entertainment venues, is policed by the CitySafe Unit. The CitySafe unit was recently credited with reducing violent crime in and around Darwin City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> Darwin has a long record of alcohol abuse and violent crime with 6,000 assaults in 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etjaw_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-etjaw-54">[51]</a></sup> of which 350 resulted in broken jaws and noses – more than anywhere else in the world, according to the Royal Darwin Hospital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etjaw_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-etjaw-54">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin is split between nine electoral divisions in the Legislative Assembly—<a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Port_Darwin" title="Electoral division of Port Darwin">Port Darwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Fannie_Bay" title="Electoral division of Fannie Bay">Fannie Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Fong_Lim" title="Electoral division of Fong Lim">Fong Lim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Nightcliff" title="Electoral division of Nightcliff">Nightcliff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Sanderson" title="Electoral division of Sanderson">Sanderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Johnston" title="Electoral division of Johnston">Johnston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Casuarina" title="Electoral division of Casuarina">Casuarina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Wanguri" title="Electoral division of Wanguri">Wanguri</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Electoral_division_of_Karama" title="Electoral division of Karama">Karama</a>. Historically, Darwin was a stronghold for the <a href="/wiki/Country_Liberal_Party" title="Country Liberal Party">Country Liberal Party</a>. However, since the turn of the century, <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Labor</a> has been much more competitive, particularly in the more diverse northern section.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Supreme_Court.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/The_Supreme_Court.JPG/225px-The_Supreme_Court.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/The_Supreme_Court.JPG/338px-The_Supreme_Court.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/The_Supreme_Court.JPG/450px-The_Supreme_Court.JPG 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Supreme_Court.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Supreme Court in the city centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The two largest economic sectors are <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>. Mining and energy industry production exceeds $2.5 billion per annum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> The most important mineral resources are gold, zinc and <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a> and many others. The energy production is mostly off shore with <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Sea" title="Timor Sea">Timor Sea</a>, although there are significant <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> deposits near Darwin. Tourism employs 8% of Darwin residents, and is expected to grow as domestic and international tourists are now spending time in Darwin during the <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">Wet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">Dry</a> seasons. Federal spending is a major contributor to the local economy as well.</p>
<p>The military presence that is maintained both within Darwin, and the wider Northern Territory, is a substantial source of employment.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_CBD-2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Darwin_CBD-2005.jpg/220px-Darwin_CBD-2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Darwin_CBD-2005.jpg/330px-Darwin_CBD-2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Darwin_CBD-2005.jpg/440px-Darwin_CBD-2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_CBD-2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Darwin CBD (Central Business District), circa 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Darwin's importance as a port is expected to grow, due to the increased exploitation of petroleum in the nearby Timor Sea, and to the completion of the railway link and continued expansion in trade with Asia. During 2005, a number of major construction projects started in Darwin. One is the redevelopment of the Wharf Precinct, which includes a large convention and exhibition centre, apartment housing including <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_Pandanas" title="Outrigger Pandanas">Outrigger Pandanas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evolution_on_Gardiner" title="Evolution on Gardiner">Evolution on Gardiner</a>, retail and entertainment outlets including a large wave pool and safe swimming lagoon. The <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatown</a> project has also started with plans to construct multi-level carparks and Chinese-themed retail and dining outlets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_the_Northern_Territory" title="List of schools in the Northern Territory">List of schools in the Northern Territory</a></div>
<p>Education is overseen territory-wide by the Department of Education and Training (DET), whose role is to continually improve education outcomes for all students, with a focus on Indigenous students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Preschool,_primary_and_secondary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Preschool.2C_primary_and_secondary">Preschool, primary and secondary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Preschool, primary and secondary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Darwin is served by a number of public and private schools that cater to local and overseas students. Over 16,500 primary and secondary students are enrolled in schools in Darwin, with 10,524 students attending primary education, and 5,932 students attending secondary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABS_Education_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABS_Education-58">[55]</a></sup> There are over 12,089 students enrolled in government schools and 2,124 students enrolled in independent schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABS_Education_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-ABS_Education-58">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CDU_library,_Casuarina.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1839" data-file-width="2453" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/CDU_library%2C_Casuarina.jpg/220px-CDU_library%2C_Casuarina.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/CDU_library%2C_Casuarina.jpg/330px-CDU_library%2C_Casuarina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/CDU_library%2C_Casuarina.jpg/440px-CDU_library%2C_Casuarina.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CDU_library,_Casuarina.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin_University" title="Charles Darwin University">Charles Darwin University</a>'s Library</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There were 9,764 students attending schools in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Darwin" title="City of Darwin">City of Darwin</a> area. 6,045 students attended primary schools and 3,719 students attended secondary schools. There are over 7,161 students enrolled in government schools and 1,108 students enrolled in independent schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Community_id_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Community_id-59">[56]</a></sup> There are over 35 primary and pre – schools, and 12 secondary schools including both government and non-government. Most schools in the city are secular, but there are a small number of Christian, Catholic and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> institutions. Students intending to complete their secondary education can work towards either the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory_Certificate_of_Education" title="Northern Territory Certificate of Education">Northern Territory Certificate of Education</a> or the <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">International Baccalaureate</a> (only offered at <a href="/wiki/Kormilda_College" title="Kormilda College">Kormilda College</a>). Schools have been restructured into Primary, Middle and High schools since the beginning of 2007.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_and_vocational">Tertiary and vocational</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tertiary and vocational">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Darwin's largest University is the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin_University" title="Charles Darwin University">Charles Darwin University</a>, which is the central provider of tertiary education in the Northern Territory. It covers both vocational and academic courses, acting as both a university and an Institute of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technical_and_Further_Education" title="Technical and Further Education">TAFE</a>. There are over 5,500 students enrolled in tertiary and further education courses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Community_id_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Community_id-59">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation_and_culture">Recreation and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Recreation and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_2324.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="456" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Darwin_2324.jpg/220px-Darwin_2324.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Darwin_2324.jpg/330px-Darwin_2324.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Darwin_2324.jpg/440px-Darwin_2324.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_2324.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mindil Beach markets</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_and_festivals">Events and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Events and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Didgeridu_and_clap_sticks.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1264" data-file-width="1000" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Didgeridu_and_clap_sticks.jpg/220px-Didgeridu_and_clap_sticks.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Didgeridu_and_clap_sticks.jpg/330px-Didgeridu_and_clap_sticks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Didgeridu_and_clap_sticks.jpg/440px-Didgeridu_and_clap_sticks.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Didgeridu_and_clap_sticks.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Didgeridoo" title="Didgeridoo">Didgeridoo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clapstick" title="Clapstick">clapstick</a> players performing at the Seabreeze Festival</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 July, Territorians celebrate Territory Day. This is the only day of the year, apart from the Chinese New Year and New Year's Eve, when fireworks are permitted. In Darwin, the main celebrations occur at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mindil_Beach,_Northern_Territory" title="Mindil Beach, Northern Territory">Mindil Beach</a>, where a large firework display is commissioned by the government.</p>
<p>Weekly markets include Mindil Beach Sunset Markets<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup> (Thursdays and Sundays during the dry season), <a href="/wiki/Parap,_Northern_Territory" title="Parap, Northern Territory">Parap Market</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nightcliff" title="Nightcliff">Nightcliff Market</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Creek,_Northern_Territory" title="Rapid Creek, Northern Territory">Rapid Creek market</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> Mindil Beach Sunset Markets are very popular with locals and tourists alike and feature food, souvenirs, clothes and local performing artists.</p>
<p>The Darwin Festival<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> held annually, includes comedy, dance, theatre, music, film and visual art and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NT_Indigenous_Music_Awards" title="NT Indigenous Music Awards">NT Indigenous Music Awards</a>. Other festivals include the Glenti, which showcases Darwin's large Greek community, and India@Mindil, a similar festival held by the smaller Indian community. The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> is also celebrated with great festivity, highlighting the Asian influence in Darwin.</p>
<p>The Seabreeze festival, which first started in 2005, is held on the second week of May in the suburb of Nightcliff. It offers the opportunity for local talent to be showcased and a popular event is Saturday family festivities along the Nightcliff foreshore which is one of Darwin's most popular fitness tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Speargrass Festival is held annually the week prior to July's first full moon and celebrates the alternative <a href="/wiki/Top_End" title="Top End">Top End</a> lifestyle. The festival activities include music, screening of locally produced films, screen printing, basket weaving, sweat lodge, water slides, human pyramid, hot tub, frisbee golf, spear throwing, Kubb competition, bingo, communal organic cooking, morning yoga, meditation, greasy pig and healing circles. The festival occurs at the Speargrass property, 50 km (31 mi) northeast of Pine Creek<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darwin_beer-can_regatta" title="Darwin beer-can regatta">Darwin beer-can regatta</a>, held in August, celebrates Darwin's love affair with beer and contestants' race boats made exclusively of beer cans. Also in Darwin during the month of August, are the Darwin Cup horse race, and the <a href="/wiki/Rodeo" title="Rodeo">Rodeo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scylla_serrata" title="Scylla serrata">Mud Crab</a> Tying Competition.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Solar_Challenge" title="World Solar Challenge">World Solar Challenge</a> race attracts teams from around the world, most of which are fielded by universities or corporations although some are fielded by high schools. The race has a 20-year history spanning nine races, with the inaugural event taking place in 1987.</p>
<p>The Royal Darwin Show is held annually in July at the Winnellie Showgrounds. Exhibitions include agriculture and livestock. Horse events. Entertainment and side shows are also included over the 3 days of the event.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_entertainment">Arts and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Arts and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_6796.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="407" data-file-width="700" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Darwin_6796.jpg/220px-Darwin_6796.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Darwin_6796.jpg/330px-Darwin_6796.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Darwin_6796.jpg/440px-Darwin_6796.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_6796.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Darwin Festival</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Darwin_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Darwin Symphony Orchestra">Darwin Symphony Orchestra</a> was first assembled in 1989,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> and has performed throughout the Territory. The Darwin Theatre Company is a locally produced professional theatre production company, performing locally and nationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Darwin_Entertainment_Centre" title="Darwin Entertainment Centre">Darwin Entertainment Centre</a> is the city's main concert venue and hosts theatre and orchestral performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup> Other theatres include the <a href="/wiki/Darwin_Convention_Centre" title="Darwin Convention Centre">Darwin Convention Centre</a>, opened in July 2008. The Darwin Convention Centre is part of the $1.1 billion Darwin Waterfront project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin's only casino opened in 1979 as the <i>Don Casino</i> operating out of the Don Hotel on Cavenagh Street. The present site of the hotel and casino on Darwin's Mindil Beach opened in 1983 at which point gambling operations ceased at the Don Hotel and commenced at the newly built facilities. The new hotel and casino was named <i>Mindil Beach Casino</i> up until 1985 when the name changed to the <i>Diamond Beach Hotel Casino</i>. Upon the acquisition by <a href="/wiki/MGM_Resorts_International" title="MGM Resorts International">MGM Grand</a> the hotel was re-branded as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Darwin" title="MGM Grand Darwin">MGM Grand Darwin</a>, before it changed to <a href="/wiki/Skycity_Darwin" title="Skycity Darwin">Skycity Darwin</a> after <a href="/wiki/Skycity_Entertainment_Group" title="Skycity Entertainment Group">Skycity Entertainment Group</a> purchased the hotel in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_and_Art_Gallery_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="Museum and Art Gallery of the Northern Territory">Northern Territory Museum and Art Gallery</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> (MAGNT) in Darwin gives an overview of the history of the area, including exhibits on Cyclone Tracy and the boats of the Pacific Islands. The MAGNT also organises the annual Telstra National Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander Art Award, the longest running Indigenous art award in Australia. The MAGNT also manages the Defence of Darwin Experience, a multi-media installation that tells the story of the Japanese air raids on Darwin during World War II.</p>
<p>The Darwin Festival and the Darwin Fringe Festival are annual events. A range of art galleries including specialised Aboriginal art galleries are a feature of Darwin.</p>
<p>Local and visiting musical bands can be heard at venues including the <a href="/wiki/Darwin_Entertainment_Centre" title="Darwin Entertainment Centre">Darwin Entertainment Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Hotel,_Darwin" title="Victoria Hotel, Darwin">The Vic Hotel</a>, Happy Yess, and Brown's Mart. A yearly music festival, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bass_in_the_Grass" title="Bass in the Grass">Bass in the Grass</a>, is very popular with youth from the surrounding area. Artists such as <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Mauboy" title="Jessica Mauboy">Jessica Mauboy</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Groovesmiths" title="The Groovesmiths">The Groovesmiths</a> call Darwin home.</p>
<p>There have been no major films set in Darwin; however, some scenes for <i><a href="/wiki/Australia_(2008_film)" title="Australia (2008 film)">Australia</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Baz_Luhrmann" title="Baz Luhrmann">Baz Luhrmann</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Water_(2007_film)" title="Black Water (2007 film)">Black Water</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> were both shot in Darwin in 2007</p>
<p>Mitchell Street in the central business district is lined with nightclubs, takeaways, and restaurants. This is the city's entertainment hub. There are several smaller theatres, three cinema complexes (CBD, Casuarina, and Palmerston), and the Deckchair Cinema.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup> This is an open-air cinema which operates through the dry season, from April to October, and screens <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">independent</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arthouse" title="Arthouse">arthouse</a> films.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_2646.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="476" data-file-width="700" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Darwin_2646.jpg/220px-Darwin_2646.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Darwin_2646.jpg/330px-Darwin_2646.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Darwin_2646.jpg/440px-Darwin_2646.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_2646.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Casuarina Beach is popular with tourists and locals alike</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Alexander.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lake_Alexander.JPG/220px-Lake_Alexander.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lake_Alexander.JPG/330px-Lake_Alexander.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lake_Alexander.JPG/440px-Lake_Alexander.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Alexander.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lake Alexander</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city has many kilometres of wide, unpolluted beaches, including the Casuarina Beach and renowned <a href="/wiki/Mindil_Beach" title="Mindil Beach">Mindil Beach</a>, home of the Mindil Beach markets. Darwin City Council has designated an area of Casuarina Beach as a free beach which offers a designated nudist beach area since 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup> Swimming in the sea during the months of October–May should be avoided due to the presence of deadly <a href="/wiki/Box_jellyfish" title="Box jellyfish">box jellyfish</a>, known locally as stingers.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile">Saltwater crocodiles</a> are very common in all waterways surrounding Darwin and are even occasionally found swimming in Darwin Harbour and on local beaches. An active trapping program is carried out by the NT Government to limit numbers of crocodiles within the Darwin urban waterway area.</p>
<p>Fishing is one of the recreations of Darwin locals. Visitors from around the world flock to Darwin aiming to catch the prized <a href="/wiki/Barramundi" title="Barramundi">barramundi</a>, an iconic fish for the region. The <a href="/wiki/Mary_River_(Northern_Territory)" title="Mary River (Northern Territory)">Mary River</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daly_River" title="Daly River">Daly River</a>, South and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Alligator_River" title="East Alligator River">East Alligator River</a> are just a few of the water bodies where the barramundi thrive.</p>
<p>Blue-water fishing is also available off the coast of Darwin; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_mackerel" title="Spanish mackerel">Spanish mackerel</a>, Black Jewfish, <a href="/wiki/Queenfish" title="Queenfish">queenfish</a>, snapper and other varieties are all found in the area and accessible in a day trip from Darwin. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Alexander_(Northern_Territory)" title="Lake Alexander (Northern Territory)">Lake Alexander</a> is a man-made swimming lake which is located at <a href="/wiki/East_Point,_Northern_Territory" title="East Point, Northern Territory">East Point Reserve</a>. It is generally considered crocodile and jellyfish safe, however a freak outbreak of non-deadly jellyfish in 2003 caused its closure for a brief period of time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Darwin Surf Lifesaving Club<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup> operates long boats and surf skis and provides events and lifesaving accreditations.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Parks and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Darwin has extensive parks and gardens. These include the <a href="/wiki/George_Brown_Darwin_Botanic_Gardens" title="George Brown Darwin Botanic Gardens">George Brown Darwin Botanic Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Point,_Northern_Territory" title="East Point, Northern Territory">East Point Reserve</a>, Casuarina Coastal Reserve, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin_National_Park" title="Charles Darwin National Park">Charles Darwin National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knuckey_Lagoons_Conservation_Reserve" title="Knuckey Lagoons Conservation Reserve">Knuckey Lagoons Conservation Reserve</a>, Leanyer Recreation Park, the <a href="/wiki/Nightcliff,_Northern_Territory" title="Nightcliff, Northern Territory">Nightcliff</a> Foreshore, <a href="/wiki/Bicentennial_Park_(Darwin)" title="Bicentennial Park (Darwin)">Bicentennial Park</a> and the Jingili Water Gardens.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_the_Northern_Territory" title="Sport in the Northern Territory">Sport in the Northern Territory</a></div>
<p>The Marrara Sports Complex near the airport has stadiums for <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Aussie Rules</a> (<a href="/wiki/Marrara_Oval" title="Marrara Oval">TIO Stadium</a>), cricket, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, basketball (and indoor court sports), soccer, athletics and <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a>. Every two years since 1991 (excluding 2003 due to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SARS" title="SARS">SARS</a> outbreak), Darwin has played host to the <a href="/wiki/Arafura_Games" title="Arafura Games">Arafura Games</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> a major regional <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sporting event</a>. In July 2003, the city hosted its first international <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">test cricket</a> match between <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_cricket_team" title="Australia national cricket team">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_national_cricket_team" title="Bangladesh national cricket team">Bangladesh</a>, followed by Australia and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_cricket_team" title="Sri Lanka national cricket team">Sri Lanka</a> in 2004.</p>
<p>Australian-rules football is played all year round. Melbourne's <a href="/wiki/Western_Bulldogs" title="Western Bulldogs">Western Bulldogs</a> <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">Australian Football League</a> side plays one home game at Marrara Oval each year. The ATSIC <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_All-Stars_(Australian_football)" title="Indigenous All-Stars (Australian football)">Aboriginal All-Stars</a> also participate in the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">AFL</a> pre-season competition. In 2003, a record crowd of 17,500<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> attended a pre-season game between the All-Stars and <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Football_Club" title="Carlton Football Club">Carlton Football Club</a> at Marrara.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_the_Northern_Territory" title="Rugby league in the Northern Territory">Rugby League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_the_Northern_Territory" title="Rugby union in the Northern Territory">Rugby Union</a> club competitions are played in Darwin each year, organised by the NTRL and NTRU respectively. The Heineken Hottest 7s in the World tournament is hosted in Darwin each January, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rugby_Sevens" title="Rugby Sevens">Rugby Sevens</a> club teams from countries including Australia, New Zealand, Papua New Guinea, Malaysia, and Singapore competing. Darwin's Hottest 7s is the richest Rugby 7s tournament in the Southern Hemisphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hottest_7s_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hottest_7s-80">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin hosts a round of the <a href="/wiki/Supercars_Championship" title="Supercars Championship">Supercars Championship</a> every year bringing thousands of motorsports fans to the <a href="/wiki/Hidden_Valley_Raceway" title="Hidden Valley Raceway">Hidden Valley Raceway</a>. Also located Hidden Valley, adjacent to the road racing circuit, is Darwin's <a href="/wiki/Dirt_track_racing" title="Dirt track racing">Dirt track racing</a> venue, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Northline_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Northline Speedway (page does not exist)">Northline Speedway</a>. The speedway has hosted a number of Australian Championships over the years for different categories including <a href="/wiki/Australian_Sprintcar_Championship" title="Australian Sprintcar Championship">Sprintcars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australian_Speedcar_Championship" title="Australian Speedcar Championship">Speedcars</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Australian_Super_Sedan_Championship" title="Australian Super Sedan Championship">Super Sedans</a>.</p>
<p>The Darwin Cup culminating on the first Monday of August is a very popular horse race event for Darwin and draws large crowds every year to Fannie Bay Racecourse. While it is not as popular as the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cup" title="Melbourne Cup">Melbourne Cup</a>, it does draw a crowd and, in 2003, <a href="/wiki/Sky_Racing" title="Sky Racing">Sky Racing</a> began televising most of the races. The Darwin Cup day is a public holiday for the Northern Territory (<a href="/wiki/Picnic_Day_(Australian_holiday)" title="Picnic Day (Australian holiday)">Picnic Day</a> public holiday).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The-gardens-nt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="665" data-file-width="1000" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The-gardens-nt.jpg/220px-The-gardens-nt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The-gardens-nt.jpg/330px-The-gardens-nt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The-gardens-nt.jpg/440px-The-gardens-nt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The-gardens-nt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Channel Nine Darwin headquarters which is located in the inner city suburb of <a href="/wiki/The_Gardens,_Northern_Territory" title="The Gardens, Northern Territory">The Gardens</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Darwin's major newspapers are the <i><a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory_News" title="Northern Territory News">Northern Territory News</a></i> (Monday – Saturday), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Territorian" title="The Sunday Territorian">The Sunday Territorian</a></i> (Sunday), and the national daily, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Australian" title="The Australian">The Australian</a></i> (Monday–Friday) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Weekend_Australian" title="The Weekend Australian">The Weekend Australian</a></i> (Saturday), all published by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/News_Limited" title="News Limited">News Limited</a>. Free weekly community newspapers include the <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin_Sun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Darwin Sun (page does not exist)">Darwin Sun</a></i>, the <i>Litchfield Sun</i>, and <i>Palmerston Sun</i>; all published by a News Limited subsidiary.</p>
<p>Five free-to-air channels service Darwin. Commercial television channels are provided by <a href="/wiki/TND" title="TND">Southern Cross Darwin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Seven_Network" title="Seven Network">Seven Network</a> affiliate), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NTD_(television_station)" title="NTD (television station)">Channel Nine Darwin</a> (formerly branded as Channel 8) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darwin_Digital_Television" title="Darwin Digital Television">Darwin Digital Television</a> (<a href="/wiki/Network_Ten" title="Network Ten">Network Ten</a> relay), which launched on 28 April 2008. The two Government owned national broadcast services in Darwin are the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Australian Broadcasting Corporation">ABC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Special_Broadcasting_Service" title="Special Broadcasting Service">SBS</a>. Subscription Television (Pay TV) service <a href="/wiki/Austar" title="Austar">Austar</a> is available via cable in the Darwin region.</p>
<p>Darwin has radio stations on both AM and FM frequencies. ABC stations include <a href="/wiki/ABC_News_Radio" title="ABC News Radio">ABC News Radio</a> (102.5FM), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/105.7_ABC_Darwin" title="105.7 ABC Darwin">ABC Local Radio</a> (105.7FM), <a href="/wiki/Radio_National" title="Radio National">ABC Radio National</a> (657AM), <a href="/wiki/ABC_Classic_FM" title="ABC Classic FM">ABC Classic FM</a> (107.3FM) and <a href="/wiki/Triple_J" title="Triple J">Triple J</a> (103.3FM). <a href="/wiki/Special_Broadcasting_Service" title="Special Broadcasting Service">SBS</a> (100.9FM) also broadcasts its national radio network to Darwin.</p>
<p>Darwin has two commercial radio stations <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_FM" title="Hot 100 FM">Hot 100</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mix_104.9" title="Mix 104.9">Mix 104.9</a>. Other stations in Darwin include university-based station <a href="/wiki/104.1_Territory_FM" title="104.1 Territory FM">104.1 Territory FM</a>, dance music station <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KIK_FM" title="KIK FM">KIK FM</a> 91.5, Italian-language channel <a href="/wiki/Rete_Italia" title="Rete Italia">Rete Italia</a> 1611AM, community based stations includes <a href="/wiki/Radio_Larrakia" title="Radio Larrakia">Radio Larrakia</a> 94.5 and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Yolngu_Radio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Yolngu Radio (page does not exist)">Yolngu Radio</a> 1530AM and <a href="/wiki/Rhema_FM" title="Rhema FM">Rhema FM</a> 97.7.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Darwin_Hospital.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="665" data-file-width="1000" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Royal_Darwin_Hospital.JPG/220px-Royal_Darwin_Hospital.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Royal_Darwin_Hospital.JPG/330px-Royal_Darwin_Hospital.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Royal_Darwin_Hospital.JPG/440px-Royal_Darwin_Hospital.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Darwin_Hospital.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Royal Darwin Hospital</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="Government of the Northern Territory">Government of the Northern Territory</a> Department of Health and Families oversees one public hospital in the Darwin metropolitan region. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Darwin_Hospital" title="Royal Darwin Hospital">Royal Darwin Hospital</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Tiwi,_Northern_Territory" title="Tiwi, Northern Territory">Tiwi</a>, is the city's major teaching and referral hospital, and the largest in the Northern Territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is one major private hospital <b>Darwin Private Hospital</b> located at <a href="/wiki/Tiwi,_Northern_Territory" title="Tiwi, Northern Territory">Tiwi</a>, adjacent to the Royal Darwin Hospital. Darwin Private Hospital is operated and owned by <a href="/wiki/Healthscope" title="Healthscope">Healthscope Ltd</a>, a private hospital corporation.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Darwin" title="Public transport in Darwin">Public transport in Darwin</a></div>
<p>The Territory's <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120120122437/http://www.nt.gov.au/transport/public/" rel="nofollow">public transport</a> services are managed by the Department of Lands and Planning, Public Transport Division. Darwin has a bus network serviced by a range of contracted bus operators,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup> which provides transport to the main suburbs of Darwin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin has no commuter rail system; however, long-distance passenger rail services do operate out of the city. The Alice Springs to Darwin rail line was completed in 2003 linking Darwin to <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>. The first service ran in 2004. <a href="/wiki/The_Ghan" title="The Ghan">The Ghan</a> passenger train service from Adelaide via <a href="/wiki/Alice_Springs" title="Alice Springs">Alice Springs</a> and Katherine runs two to three times per week depending on the season.</p>
<table cellpadding="-1" cellspacing="0" class="wikitable" style="margin:0.5em auto; font-size:95%;clear:both; border-top: 0px none; border-collapse: separate;">
<tr>
<th style="vertical-align: middle; width: 30%; border: 1px solid #aaa; border-left: none; border-bottom: none; color:#FFFFFF; background:#CBB989;">Preceding station</th>

<td rowspan="1" style="text-align: center; vertical-align: middle; border-left: 0px none; border-bottom: 0px none; border-right: 1px #aaa solid; border-top: 1px #aaa solid;"><i>Terminus</i></td>
<td rowspan="1" style="text-align: center; border-left: 0px none; border-bottom: 0px none; border-right: 0px none; border-top: 1px #aaa solid; width: 8px; background-color: #934541"></td>

<div style="font-size: smaller;"><i>towards <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Parklands_Terminal" title="Adelaide Parklands Terminal">Adelaide</a></i></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Darwin_Airport_Terminal_opening_in_December_1991.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1176" data-file-width="1772" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/New_Darwin_Airport_Terminal_opening_in_December_1991.jpg/220px-New_Darwin_Airport_Terminal_opening_in_December_1991.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/New_Darwin_Airport_Terminal_opening_in_December_1991.jpg/330px-New_Darwin_Airport_Terminal_opening_in_December_1991.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/New_Darwin_Airport_Terminal_opening_in_December_1991.jpg/440px-New_Darwin_Airport_Terminal_opening_in_December_1991.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Darwin_Airport_Terminal_opening_in_December_1991.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Official opening of <a href="/wiki/Darwin_International_Airport" title="Darwin International Airport">Darwin International Airport</a> in 1991</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Darwin_International_Airport" title="Darwin International Airport">Darwin International Airport</a>, located in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Marrara,_Northern_Territory" title="Marrara, Northern Territory">Marrara</a>, is Darwin's only airport, which shares its runways with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Air_Force" title="Royal Australian Air Force">Royal Australian Air Force</a>'s <a href="/wiki/RAAF_Base_Darwin" title="RAAF Base Darwin">RAAF Base Darwin</a>.</p>
<p>Darwin can be reached via the <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Highway" title="Stuart Highway">Stuart Highway</a> which runs the length of the Northern Territory from Darwin through Katherine, Tennant Creek, Alice Springs and on to Adelaide. Other major roads in Darwin include, <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Brennan_Drive" title="Tiger Brennan Drive">Tiger Brennan Drive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amy_Johnson_Avenue" title="Amy Johnson Avenue">Amy Johnson Avenue</a>, Dick Ward Drive, <a href="/wiki/Bagot_Road" title="Bagot Road">Bagot Road</a>, Trower Road and McMillans Road. Bus service in the greater Darwin area is served by <a href="/wiki/Darwinbus" title="Darwinbus">Darwinbus</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Port_Darwin" title="Port Darwin">Port Darwin</a></div>
<p>Ferries leave from Port Darwin to island locations, mainly for tourists. A ferry service to the <a href="/wiki/Tiwi_Islands" title="Tiwi Islands">Tiwi Islands</a>, the <i>Arafura Pearl</i> operates from Cullen Bay.</p>
<p>Darwin has a new <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_deep_water_ports&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="List of deep water ports (page does not exist)">deepwater</a> port, East Arm Wharf, which opened in 2000. It has 754-metres of wharfline and is capable of handling <a href="/wiki/Panamax" title="Panamax">Panamax</a>-sized ships of a maximum length of 274 metres and a <a href="/wiki/Deadweight_tonnage" title="Deadweight tonnage">DWT</a> of up to 80,000 <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Water storage, supply and Power for Darwin is managed by <a href="/wiki/Power_and_Water_Corporation" title="Power and Water Corporation">Power and Water Corporation</a>, which is owned by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="Government of the Northern Territory">Government of the Northern Territory</a>. The corporation is also responsible for management of sewage and the major water catchments in the region. Water is mainly stored in the largest dam, The <a href="/wiki/Darwin_River_Dam" title="Darwin River Dam">Darwin River Dam</a> which holds up to 90% of Darwin's water supply. For many years, Darwin's principal water supply came from Manton Dam.</p>
<p>Darwin, its suburbs, Palmerston and <a href="/wiki/Katherine,_Northern_Territory" title="Katherine, Northern Territory">Katherine</a> are powered by the Channel Island Power Station, the largest power plant in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a>.</p>
<p>A new power plant, the Weddell Power Station, is near completion. The first two generators came on line in 2008–09. The third generator is due to be completed in 2011–12. When the power station is fully operational, it will add 30% capacity to Darwin's power supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Darwin_National_Park.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Charles_Darwin_National_Park.jpg/220px-Charles_Darwin_National_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Charles_Darwin_National_Park.jpg/330px-Charles_Darwin_National_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Charles_Darwin_National_Park.jpg/440px-Charles_Darwin_National_Park.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Darwin_National_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Picnic area located <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin_National_Park" title="Charles Darwin National Park">Charles Darwin National Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tourism is one of Darwin's largest industries. Tourism is a major industry and employment sector for the Northern Territory. In 2005/06, 1.38 million people visited the Northern Territory. They stayed for 9.2 million nights and spent over $1.5 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup> The tourism industry directly employed 8,391 Territorians in June 2006 and when indirect employment is included, tourism typically accounts for more than 14,000 jobs across the Territory.</p>
<p>Darwin is a hub for tours to <a href="/wiki/Kakadu_National_Park" title="Kakadu National Park">Kakadu National Park</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Litchfield_National_Park" title="Litchfield National Park">Litchfield National Park</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Katherine_Gorge" title="Katherine Gorge">Katherine Gorge</a>. The Territory is traditionally divided into the wet and dry, but there are up to six traditional seasons in Darwin. It is warm and sunny from May to September. Humidity rises during the green season, from October to April bringing thunderstorms and monsoonal rains which rejuvenates the landscape. Tourism is largely seasonal with most tourists visiting during the cooler dry season which runs from April to September.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation_history">Aviation history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Aviation history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_1921.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="461" data-file-width="700" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Darwin_1921.jpg/220px-Darwin_1921.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Darwin_1921.jpg/330px-Darwin_1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Darwin_1921.jpg/440px-Darwin_1921.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darwin_1921.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Darwin Aviation Heritage Centre – 1st Ultralight – Hover Bird</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Darwin has played host to many of aviation's early pioneers. On 10 December 1919 Captain <a href="/wiki/Ross_Macpherson_Smith" title="Ross Macpherson Smith">Ross Smith</a> and his crew landed in Darwin and won a £10,000 Prize from the Australian Government for completing the first flight from London to Australia in under thirty days. Smith and his Crew flew a <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Vimy" title="Vickers Vimy">Vickers Vimy</a>, G-EAOU and landed on an airstrip that has now become Ross Smith Avenue.</p>
<p>Other aviation pioneers include <a href="/wiki/Amy_Johnson" title="Amy Johnson">Amy Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Earhart" title="Amelia Earhart">Amelia Earhart</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Charles_Kingsford_Smith" title="Charles Kingsford Smith">Charles Kingsford Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bert_Hinkler" title="Bert Hinkler">Bert Hinkler</a>. The original QANTAS Empire Airways Ltd Hangar, a registered heritage site,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup> was part of the original Darwin Civil Aerodrome in Parap and is now a museum and still bears scars from the <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Darwin" title="Bombing of Darwin">bombing of Darwin</a> during World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin was home to Australian and US pilots during the war, with air strips being built in and around Darwin. Today Darwin provides a staging ground for <a href="/wiki/Military_exercise" title="Military exercise">military exercises</a>.</p>
<p>Darwin was a compulsory stop over/check point in the London to Melbourne Centenary Air Race in 1934. The official name of the race was the <a href="/wiki/MacRobertson_Air_Race" title="MacRobertson Air Race">MacRobertson Air Race</a>. Winners of the great race were <a href="/wiki/Tom_Campbell_Black" title="Tom Campbell Black">Tom Campbell Black</a> and <a href="/wiki/C._W._A._Scott" title="C. W. A. Scott">C. W. A. Scott</a>.</p>
<p>The following is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i> magazine</a>, 29 October 1934, Volume XXIV, Number 18.</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Third Day. Biggest sensation of the race came just before dawn on the third day, when burly Lieutenant Scott and dapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight_Lieutenant" title="Flight Lieutenant">Captain</a> Black flew their scarlet <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_DH.88" title="De Havilland DH.88">Comet</a> into Darwin. They had covered the last 300 miles over water on one motor, risked death landing on a field made soggy by the first rain in seven months. Said sandy-haired Lieutenant Scott: "We've had a devil of a trip." But they had flown 9000 miles in two days, had broken the England to Australia record of 162 hr. in the unbelievable time of 52hr. 33 min., were only 2000 miles from their goal at Melbourne.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Australian Aviation Heritage Centre is located approximately 8 km (5 mi) from the City centre on the Stuart Highway and is one of only two places outside the United States where a B52 bomber (on permanent loan from the United States Air Force) is on public display.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="US_military_presence">US military presence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: US military presence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Quadrilateral_Security_Dialogue" title="Quadrilateral Security Dialogue">Quadrilateral Security Dialogue</a></div>
<p>On 16 November 2011, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Julia_Gillard" title="Julia Gillard">Julia Gillard</a> and President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> announced that the United States would station troops in Australia for the first time since World War II. The agreement between the United States and Australia would involve a contingent of 250 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Marine_Corps" title="US Marine Corps">Marines</a> arriving in Darwin in 2012, with the total number rising to a maximum of 2,500 troops by 2017 on six-month rotations as well as a supporting air element including F-22 Raptors, F-35 Joint Strike Fighters and KC-135 refuelers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup> China and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> have expressed concern about the decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup> Some analysts have argued that an expanded U.S. presence could pose a threat to security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup> Gillard announced that the first 200 U.S. Marines had arrived in Darwin from <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> on late 3 April 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> In 2013, further news of other expansion vectors was aired in USA media,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> with no comment or confirmation from Australian authorities. The agreement between the two governments remains hidden from public scrutiny.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> Marine numbers based in Darwin have increased to more than 1150 troops by 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Darwin hosts biennial multi-nation exercises named "Pitch Black";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> in 2014 this involved military personnel from Australia, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/City_of_Darwin" title="City of Darwin">City of Darwin</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Darwin,_Northern_Territory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The story around the pole holes is commonly perpetuated, though no first hand accounts have been uncovered to authenticate this</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1872 it was reported that <i>A great many statements have been made about gold being found in holes of the telegraph post, and other unimaginable places. Such statements are incorrect, and given out by interested parties.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">nearest first hand account is of linesmen finding gold near the telegraph line</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>
